<div id="review_294483947" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/294483947" />
    <a title="Katrice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7459924-katrice"><img alt="Katrice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529642409p2/7459924.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/294483947?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrice" href="/user/show/7459924-katrice">Katrice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer294483947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16725144307861813286">So this is actually the first of a two-book series of Gothic young adult tales dealing with vampires.<br/><br/>First, let me say am happy to report that, these vampires do not sparkle. In fact if that's the kind of vampire story your interested in, do not pick up this book or the other one "The Kiss of Death".<br/><br/>Both books in this series are good old Gothic horror tales of creepy things that go bump in the night. The protagonists are good hearted and initially completely overwhelmed by the horrors that are s</span>
  <span id="freeText16725144307861813286" style="display:none">So this is actually the first of a two-book series of Gothic young adult tales dealing with vampires.<br /><br />First, let me say am happy to report that, these vampires do not sparkle. In fact if that's the kind of vampire story your interested in, do not pick up this book or the other one "The Kiss of Death".<br /><br />Both books in this series are good old Gothic horror tales of creepy things that go bump in the night. The protagonists are good hearted and initially completely overwhelmed by the horrors that are slowly changing their once quite lives. Tensions rise and the protagonists rise to the occasion to do battle against the supernatural forces that threaten to overwhelm them.<br /><br />In an afterwards, the author actually states that he deliberately tried to go back to the old vampire mythos from the Carpathians, where the original tales came from and I must say he does a good job. Some of the mythos he incorporates in his own tale are "new"or ""newish"to me but they just make his own tale more compelling and the atmosphere more creepy.<br /><br />All in all its a pretty good tale with just the right amount of delicious creep factor to be appropriate for the YA crowd. There's even a nice bit of age-appropriate romance factor to it. And best of all its WELL WRITTEN. No clunky cliches or awkward phrasing. The words build an atmosphere and paint a picture, sucking you into the tale.<br /><br />Would recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16725144307861813286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_956707281" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956707281" />
    <a title="Leslee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4902013-leslee"><img alt="Leslee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595449121p2/4902013.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/956707281?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslee" href="/user/show/4902013-leslee">Leslee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4902013-leslee?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4902013-leslee?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer956707281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6910069046470619826">A delightful little novella that calls to mind earlier, darker Grimm's fairy tales before they were sanitized for children's consumption. Sedgwick plays with old European superstitions remarkably well and I was reading this I thought how wonderfully this would do as a dark fairy tale movie that's become so popular these days a la <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1735898/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Snow White and the Huntsman</a>, only done much better. <br/><br/>I think a good comparison to this novella would be as the young adult version of Angela Carter's excellent feminist </span>
  <span id="freeText6910069046470619826" style="display:none">A delightful little novella that calls to mind earlier, darker Grimm's fairy tales before they were sanitized for children's consumption. Sedgwick plays with old European superstitions remarkably well and I was reading this I thought how wonderfully this would do as a dark fairy tale movie that's become so popular these days a la <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1735898/" rel="nofollow noopener">Snow White and the Huntsman</a>, only done much better. <br /><br />I think a good comparison to this novella would be as the young adult version of Angela Carter's excellent feminist fairy tale reworkings in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49011.The_Bloody_Chamber_and_Other_Stories" title="The Bloody Chamber and Other Stories by Angela Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bloody Chamber and Other Stories</a>, a book that captivated me when I first read it in my later teens, and then captivated me again in Neil Jordan's excellent film adaptation <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Company_of_Wolves" rel="nofollow noopener">The Company of Wolves</a>, which to me hands down is still the best movie version of a dark fairy tale made to date. I'd very happily suggest this book to any fans of vampires that want to get away from the sparkly pretty boy or the goth punk that seems so popular these days. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6910069046470619826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yp/5HbxsN9pSB5NX5FUUZpD/mNTHlVUGvmLDB/q+AthfsU7XlXp+HxZP84xthfVVy0BdTVK/gfX9rkYTl0j5pQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Written by two-time National Book Award finalist Patricia McCormick, author of Sold and Never Fall Down and coauthor of the young reader’s edition of I Am Malala.\n\nIt was April 5, 1943, and the Gestapo would arrive any minute. Dietrich Bonhoeffer had been expecting this day for a long time. He had put his papers in order—and left a few notes specifically for Hitler’s men to see. Two SS agents climbed the stairs and told the boyish-looking Bonhoeffer to come with them. He calmly said good-bye to his parents, put his Bible under his arm, and left. Upstairs there was proof, in his own handwriting, that this quiet young minister was part of a conspiracy to kill Adolf Hitler.\n\nThis compelling, brilliantly researched account includes the remarkable discovery that Bonhoeffer was one of the first people to provide evidence to the Allies that Jews were being deported to death camps. It takes readers from his privileged early childhood to the studies and travel that would introduce him to peace activists around the world—eventually putting this gentle, scholarly pacifist on a deadly course to assassinate one of the most ruthless dictators in history. The Plot to Kill Hitler provides fascinating insights into what makes someone stand up for what’s right when no one else is standing with you. It is a question that every generation must answer again <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17323558576374583644">Marcus Sedgwick was born in Kent, England. Marcus is a British author and illustrator as well as a musician. He is the author of several books, including <i>Witch Hill</i> and <i>The Book of Dead Days</i>, both of which were nominated for the Edgar Allan Poe Award. The most recent of these nominations rekindled a fascination with Poe that has borne fruit here in (in <i>The Restless Dead</i>, 2007) the form of "The Hea</span>
  <span id="freeText17323558576374583644" style="display:none">Marcus Sedgwick was born in Kent, England. Marcus is a British author and illustrator as well as a musician. He is the author of several books, including <i>Witch Hill</i> and <i>The Book of Dead Days</i>, both of which were nominated for the Edgar Allan Poe Award. The most recent of these nominations rekindled a fascination with Poe that has borne fruit here in (in <i>The Restless Dead</i>, 2007) the form of "The Heart of Another" - inspired by Poe's "The Tell-Tale Heart." Of his story, Sedgwick says, "This was one of those stories that I thought might be a novel originally but actually was much better suited to the tight form of the short story. I had the initial idea some years ago but was just waiting for the right ingredient to come along. Poe's story, as well as his own fascination with technique, provided that final piece of the puzzle."<br /><br />He used to play for two bands namely playing the drums for Garrett and as the guitarist in an ABBA tribute group. He has published novels such as <i>Floodland</i> (winner of the Branford Boase Award in 2001) and <i>The Dark Horse</i> (shortlisted for The Guardian Children's Book Award 2002).</span>

Marko and Sorrel meet in Venice for the first time. They must uncover the mystery of what has happened both to Sorrel\'s father, plagued by a strange madness that prevents him from sleeping, and to Marko\'s father, a doctor, who has mysteriously gone missing after travelling to Venice to help his old friend. Years on from My Swordhand is Singing and Peter is still on the trail of the Shadow Queen. His search leads him to Venice, a city whose beauty disguises many ugly secrets. The Shadow Queen is there, gathering strength, recruiting a new army of the Undead for a final confrontation. This fabled city with its lapping waterways, its crumbling magnificence, dark, twisting alleyways and surprising piazzas is the perfect setting for Marcus\'s captivating gothic novel of love and loss         } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_3607394').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_3607394').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_3607394').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
